<div>

<p align="right" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:right;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Exhibit
99.1</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="4" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:14.0pt;">Apple Reports First Quarter Results</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">Quarterly Revenue
&amp; Net Income Highest in Apple&#146;s History</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">CUPERTINO, California&#151;January 12, 2005&#151;Apple&#174;
today announced financial results for its fiscal 2005 first quarter ended
December 25, 2004. For the quarter, the Company posted a net profit of $295
million, or $.70 per diluted share. These results compare to a net profit of
$63 million, or $.17 per diluted share, in the year-ago quarter. Revenue for
the quarter was $3.49 billion, up 74 percent from the year-ago quarter. Gross
margin was 28.5 percent, up from 26.7 percent in the year-ago quarter.
International sales accounted for 41 percent of the quarter&#146;s revenue.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Apple shipped 1,046,000 Macintosh&#174; units and
4,580,000 iPods during the quarter, representing a 26 percent increase in CPU
units and a 525 percent increase in iPods over the year-ago quarter.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#147;We are thrilled to report the highest
quarterly revenue and net income in Apple&#146;s history,&#148; said Steve Jobs, Apple&#146;s
CEO. &#147;We&#146;ve sold over 10 million iPods to date and are kicking off the new year
with a slate of innovative new products including iPod shuffle, Mac mini and
iLife &#145;05.&#148;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#147;We&#146;re pleased to report 74 percent revenue
growth, 26 percent Mac unit growth and 525 percent iPod unit growth,&#148; said Peter
Oppenheimer, Apple&#146;s CFO.&#160; &#147;Looking ahead
to the second quarter of fiscal 2005, we expect revenue of about $2.9 billion
and earnings per diluted share of about $.40.&#148;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Apple will provide live streaming of its Q1
2005 financial results conference call utilizing QuickTime&#153;, Apple&#146;s
standards-based technology for live and on-demand audio and video streaming.
The live webcast will begin at 2:00 p.m. PST on Wednesday, January 12, 2005 at
http://www.apple.com/quicktime/qtv/earningsq105/ and will also be available for
replay. The QuickTime player is available free for Macintosh and Windows users
at www.apple.com/quicktime.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">This press release contains forward-looking
statements about the Company&#146;s estimated revenue and earnings for the second
quarter of fiscal 2005. These statements involve risks and uncertainties and
actual results may differ. Potential risks and uncertainties include</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

</div>
<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='',FILE='C:\JMS\eschaeffer\05-1308-2\task272344\1308-2-ka.htm',USER='eschaef',CD='Jan 11 21:20 2005' -->


<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">continued competitive pressures in the
marketplace; the effect competitive and economic factors and the Company&#146;s
reaction to them may have on consumer and business buying decisions with
respect to the Company&#146;s products; the ability of the Company to make timely
delivery of new programs, products and successful technological innovations to
the marketplace; the continued availability of certain components and services
essential to the Company&#146;s business currently obtained by the Company from sole
or limited sources, including the timely resolution of manufacturing issues
associated with the G5 microprocessors used in many of the Company&#146;s Macintosh
systems; possible disruption in commercial activities caused by terrorist
activity and armed conflict, such as changes in logistics and security
arrangements, and reduced end-user purchases relative to expectations; possible
disruption in commercial activity as a result of natural disasters or major
health concerns including epidemics; risks associated with the Company&#146;s retail
initiative including significant investment cost, uncertain consumer acceptance
and potential impact on existing reseller relationships; the effect that the
Company&#146;s dependency on manufacturing and logistics services provided by
third-parties may have on the quality, quantity or cost of products
manufactured or services rendered; the Company&#146;s reliance on the availability
of third-party music content, and the ability of the Company to successfully
evolve its operating system and attract sufficient Macintosh developers. More
information on potential factors that could affect the Company&#146;s financial
results is included from time to time in the Company&#146;s public reports filed
with the SEC, including the Company&#146;s Form 10-K for the fiscal year ended
September 25, 2004 and the Company&#146;s Form 10-Q for the quarter ended December
25, 2004 to be filed with the SEC.&#160; The
Company assumes no obligation to update any forward-looking statements or
information, which speak as of their respective dates.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Apple ignited the personal computer revolution
in the 1970s with the Apple II and reinvented the personal computer in the
1980s with the Macintosh. Today, Apple continues to lead the industry in
innovation with its award-winning desktop and notebook computers, OS X
operating system, and iLife and professional applications. Apple is also
spearheading the digital music revolution with its iPod portable music players
and iTunes online music store.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:8.0pt;">(1)&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; Other Segments include Asia Pacific
and FileMaker.</font></p>
